# BattleRobots â€” Project Roadmap

## Vision
A physics-driven robot combat game built in Unity. Players assemble modular robots,
enter battle arenas, earn currency from wins, and unlock upgraded parts. All physics
uses ArticulationBody exclusively. The economy, save system, and event bus are SO-driven.

---

## Architecture Rules (enforced every session)
- **ArticulationBody only** â€” never Rigidbody for robot parts
- **No heap allocations** in Update / FixedUpdate
- **SO Event Channels** for all cross-component communication
- **SO assets immutable at runtime** â€” write only through designated mutator methods
- **XOR SaveSystem** for all persistence (MatchRecord, Wallet snapshot)
- **BattleRobots.UI** must never reference **BattleRobots.Physics**
- **PlayerWallet**: SO for runtime state, MatchRecord for persistence
- Namespaces: `BattleRobots.Core` / `BattleRobots.Physics` / `BattleRobots.UI` / `BattleRobots.Editor`

---

## Milestones

| # | Milestone | Target | Status |
|---|-----------|--------|--------|
| M1 | Core Foundation (SO bus, wallet, save) | Sprint 1 | **Done** |
| M2 | Robot Assembly & ArticulationBody Joints | Sprint 2 | **Done** |
| M3 | Combat Arena + Damage System | Sprint 3 | **Done** |
| M4 | Economy & Shop UI | Sprint 4 | **Done** |
| M5 | Match Loop + Win/Loss Flow | Sprint 5 | **Done** |
| M6 | Polish, VFX, Audio | Sprint 6 | **Done** |
| M7 | Meta-loop Depth (loot drops, progression bonuses, build validation) | Sprint 7 | **Done** |
| M8 | Competitive Depth & QoL (leaderboard, score history, UX improvements) | Sprint 8 | **Done** |
| M9 | Career Insights & Adaptive Engagement (career highlights, difficulty advisor, session summary) | Sprint 9 | **Done** |
| M10 | Endless Replayability (prestige system, build code sharing, match event timeline) | Sprint 10 | **Done** |
| M11 | Tutorial & Onboarding (step-by-step overlay, progress persistence, skip/advance flow) | Sprint 11 | **Done** |
| M12 | Wave Survival Mode (endless escalating bot waves, best-wave tracking, HUD, persistence) | Sprint 12 | **In Progress** |

## Session Handoff

**Last completed:** T132 (SurvivalMatchManager â€” M12 bridge component that wires _onWaveCompleted â†’ HandleWaveCompleted (award WaveConfigSO.GetRewardForWave credits, persist BestWave, advance via StartNextWave) and _onPlayerDeath â†’ HandlePlayerDeath (EndSurvival + persist BestWave); StartSurvival() public entry point; PersistBestWave() loadâ†’mutateâ†’save; 19 new EditMode tests). **2438 total tests across 176 test files.** T001â€“T132 Done. M1â€“M11 complete; M12 In Progress (T131+T132 done, T133+ pending).

**WaveController wiring (T131) â€” Editor-session steps:**
1. Create `WaveConfigSO` asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Wave â–¶ WaveConfig.
   - Set `_baseBotsPerWave`, `_botCountIncrement`, `_maxBotsPerWave` to taste (defaults: 1/1/10).
   - Set `_baseWaveReward` (default 50) and `_bonusRewardPerWave` (default 10).
   - Optionally assign `_roster` â†’ OpponentRosterSO to cycle per-wave opponent profiles.
2. Create `WaveManagerSO` asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Wave â–¶ WaveManagerSO.
   - Assign `_onWaveStarted`, `_onWaveCompleted`, `_onSurvivalEnded` â†’ new VoidGameEvent SOs.
3. Wire `GameBootstrapper` MB (Wave Survival optional header): `_waveManager` â†’ the WaveManagerSO asset.
4. Add `WaveController` MB to the Arena/HUD canvas:
   - `_waveManager` â†’ the WaveManagerSO asset.
   - `_onWaveStarted`, `_onWaveCompleted` â†’ the corresponding VoidGameEvents.
   - `_onSurvivalEnded` â†’ the corresponding VoidGameEvent.
   - `_survivalPanel` â†’ the root HUD panel for survival mode.
   - `_waveLabel`, `_botsLabel`, `_bestWaveLabel` â†’ Text components inside the panel.
5. In your survival game logic, call:
   - `WaveManagerSO.StartSurvival(config)` to begin a run.
   - `WaveManagerSO.RecordBotDefeated()` each time a bot is destroyed.
   - `WaveManagerSO.StartNextWave(config)` after _onWaveCompleted fires.
   - `WaveManagerSO.EndSurvival()` when the player's robot is destroyed.
6. Persist BestWave: in your EndMatch/EndSurvival handler, call
   `save.survivalBestWave = _waveManager.BestWave` before SaveSystem.Save(save).
7. Play-test: start survival â†’ HUD shows "Wave 1", N bots; defeat bots â†’ wave counter increments; player defeated â†’ HUD hides; relaunch â†’ best-wave label shows persisted record.

**Next recommended tasks for M12 (Wave Survival Mode):**
- **T132**: SurvivalMatchManager â€” replaces/extends MatchManager for survival sessions; awards credits per wave (WaveConfigSO.GetRewardForWave); triggers WaveManagerSO.StartNextWave after _onWaveCompleted; triggers EndSurvival on player death; persists BestWave to SaveData.
- **T133**: SurvivalResultsController â€” post-survival summary panel (waves completed, total bots defeated, credits earned, new best-wave badge); subscribes _onSurvivalEnded; reads WaveManagerSO + PlayerWallet.

**Next action:** Implement T133 (SurvivalResultsController) â€” the post-survival summary panel that reads WaveManagerSO + PlayerWallet on _onSurvivalEnded and shows waves completed, total bots defeated, credits earned this run, and a new best-wave badge.

**PartRepairManager wiring (T107) â€” Editor-session steps:**

   - Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Combat â–¶ PartConditionRegistry.

   - Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Combat â–¶ PartRepairConfig.
   - Set `_creditsPerHPPoint` (default 2.0 = 100 credits to restore a fully destroyed 50-HP part).
   - Tune higher to make the repair economy more of a credits-sink.

   - Assign `_registry`     â†’ the `PartConditionRegistry` asset created above.
   - Assign `_wallet`       â†’ the `PlayerWallet` SO asset.

   as the `PartConditionRegistry` (they share the same SO references):
   - In `PartHealthSystem._parts`, each `PartEntry.condition` should point to the same

   - Add one `RarityTierData` entry per rarity tier (list order does not matter):
     - Common:    displayName "Common",    tintColor grey,   lootWeightMultiplier 1.0
     - Uncommon:  displayName "Uncommon",  tintColor green,  lootWeightMultiplier 0.7
     - Rare:      displayName "Rare",      tintColor blue,   lootWeightMultiplier 0.4
     - Epic:      displayName "Epic",      tintColor purple, lootWeightMultiplier 0.2
     - Legendary: displayName "Legendary", tintColor yellow, lootWeightMultiplier 0.1
2. Assign `PartRarity` in the Inspector for each `PartDefinition` asset:
   - Common parts (starter weapons, basic chassis) stay at PartRarity.Common.
   - Tune rarity upwards for stronger stat parts.
3. Upgrade `LootDropManager` to use rarity-weighted drops:
   - In `HandleMatchEnded`, replace `_lootTable.RollDrop(lootSeed)` with
     `_lootTable.RollDrop(lootSeed, _rarityConfig)` â€” assign a new
     optional `_rarityConfig` field to the LootDropManager in the Inspector.
   - (Note: LootDropManager currently calls the base overload; the rarity-aware
     overload exists on LootTableSO but LootDropManager has not been patched â€”
     this Inspector wiring is optional until LootDropManager is patched next session.)
4. On each `ShopItemController` prefab (optional):
   - Assign `_rarityConfig` â†’ the PartRarityConfig asset.
   - Assign `_rarityBadge` â†’ an Image on the row prefab for rarity tinting.
   - Assign `_rarityLabel` â†’ a Text element showing the rarity name.

**LootDrop wiring (T101) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ highest priority
1. Create `LootTableSO` asset:
   - Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ LootTable.

   - Set `_winDropChance` (default 0.3 = 30 % chance per win).

   - Add `LootDropManager` MB.
   - Assign `_lootTable` â†’ the LootTableSO created above.

   - Assign `_onMatchEnded` â†’ the same VoidGameEvent as MatchManager._onMatchEnded.
   - Optionally assign `_notificationQueue` â†’ NotificationQueueSO for "Loot Drop!" toasts.
3. No further wiring required â€” the manager auto-subscribes on OnEnable and
   awards drops only for parts the player does not yet own.

**BotPersonality wiring (T087) â€” Editor-session steps:**

**C# layer status:** Complete and compiles clean. Session 45 added T087 â€” AI behavior personality variants. `BotPersonalitySO` defines 5 personality archetypes (Balanced/Aggressive/Defensive/Berserker/Tactical) via 4 runtime-modifier fields (AttackCooldownMultiplier, DetectionRangeDelta, AttackRangeDelta, FacingThresholdMultiplier). `RobotAIController.Awake()` applies the personality AFTER difficulty config so the two systems stack correctly; all field clamps (`Mathf.Max`) prevent illegal values; zero alloc, no new FSM states.

**BotPersonality wiring (T087) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ new, first priority
1. Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ BotPersonality.
   Set `_personalityType` to the desired archetype (informational only).
   Configure the four modifier fields:
   - `_attackCooldownMultiplier` â€” 0.5 for Aggressive (faster attacks), 1.5 for Defensive (slower).
   - `_detectionRangeDelta` â€” +5 for Defensive (wider awareness), âˆ’3 for Aggressive (must close in).
   - `_attackRangeDelta` â€” +2 for Tactical/Defensive (engages from further away).
   - `_facingThresholdMultiplier` â€” 2.0 for Berserker/Tactical (wide aiming cone).
2. On the enemy robot's root GameObject, add/select the `RobotAIController` component.
3. Assign `_botPersonality` â†’ the BotPersonalitySO asset created above.
   Leave null for neutral (Balanced) behavior.
4. The personality is applied once in `Awake()` after any `BotDifficultyConfig`/`SelectedDifficultySO`
   override â€” no additional code needed.

**C# layer status:** Complete and compiles clean. Session 44 added T086 â€” visual hit-flash feedback for robots. `DamageFlashController` subscribes to the same `FloatGameEvent` wired into `HealthSO._onHealthChanged`; detects damage by comparing the incoming health against `_previousHealth`; drives all child `Renderer`s via a shared `MaterialPropertyBlock` (zero material instantiation); uses `WaitForSecondsRealtime` (pause-safe). Falls back to 0.15 s / red when no `DamageFlashConfig` SO is assigned.

**C# layer status:** Complete and compiles clean. Session 42 added T084 â€” the daily-challenge engagement system. Reuses `BonusConditionSO` as challenge types; deterministic date-based selection ensures all players see the same challenge each day. `DailyChallengeManager` evaluates the condition after every match via `MatchEndBonusEvaluator.EvaluateCondition()` and credits `BonusAmount أ— RewardMultiplier` to the wallet on success. `SaveData` extended with three backwards-compatible fields.

**DamageFlash wiring (T086) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ new, first priority
1. Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Combat â–¶ DamageFlashConfig.
   Set `_flashColor` (e.g. red for player, yellow for enemy) and `_flashDuration` (0.15 s default).
   One global instance is fine; assign the same asset to both robots or create per-robot variants.
2. On each robot's root GameObject (alongside `DamageReceiver`), add `DamageFlashController` MB.
3. Assign `_health` â†’ the robot's HealthSO asset.
4. Assign `_onHealthChanged` â†’ the same `FloatGameEvent` SO that is wired inside that HealthSO
   (the one also consumed by `CombatHUDController._onPlayerHealthChanged` / `_onEnemyHealthChanged`).
5. Assign `_config` â†’ the DamageFlashConfig SO from step 1 (leave null to use built-in 0.15 s/red default).
6. The effect is automatic: every time `HealthSO.ApplyDamage` is called, all child Renderers on
   the robot briefly tint to the flash colour and then revert â€” no additional code needed.

**ChallengeProgressHUD wiring (T085) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ new, first priority

   (e.g. alongside CombatHUDController on the Arena HUD).

     `_challengeNameText`    â†’ Text showing the challenge display name
     `_challengeProgressText`â†’ Text showing live progress ("47 / 80", "12s / 30s", etc.)
     `_completedText`        â†’ Text showing "COMPLETE!" once IsCompleted = true

**DailyChallenge wiring (T084) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ new, first priority
1. Create SO assets:
   - `DailyChallengeConfig`: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ DailyChallengeConfig.
     Add `BonusConditionSO` assets to `_challengePool`.  Suggested starter conditions:
     - "Perfect Shield": NoDamageTaken, Threshold=0, BonusAmount=100
     - "Speed Run": WonUnderDuration, Threshold=30, BonusAmount=75
     - "Destroyer": DamageDealtExceeds, Threshold=80, BonusAmount=50
     - "Efficiency Master": DamageEfficiency, Threshold=0.8, BonusAmount=60
     Set `_rewardMultiplier` = 2 (double the normal match bonus).
   - `DailyChallengeSO`: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ DailyChallengeSO.
     Create a `VoidGameEvent` SO for `_onChallengeCompleted`.
2. In the Bootstrap scene, add `DailyChallengeManager` MB:
   - Assign `_dailyChallenge` â†’ the DailyChallengeSO.
   - Assign `_config` â†’ the DailyChallengeConfig.
   - Assign `_matchResult` â†’ the MatchResultSO (same one used by PostMatchController).
   - Assign `_onMatchEnded` â†’ the MatchEnded VoidGameEvent.
   - Assign `_playerWallet` â†’ the PlayerWallet SO.
   - Optionally assign `_notificationQueue` for a toast on completion.
3. In the GameBootstrapper, assign `_dailyChallenge` â†’ the DailyChallengeSO.
4. In any pre-match or main-menu scene, add `DailyChallengeController` MB to a panel:
   - Assign `_dailyChallenge`, `_config`, `_onChallengeCompleted`.
   - Wire optional `_titleText`, `_descriptionText`, `_rewardText`, `_completedBadge`.

**PostMatchBonusDisplay wiring (T083) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ new, first priority
1. On the PostMatchController in the Arena scene, assign the following optional fields:
   - `_bonusEarnedText` â†’ a Text element that will show "Bonus: +175" or "Bonus: none".
   - `_bonusDetailText` â†’ a multiline Text element showing the per-condition breakdown.
   - `_bonusCatalog` â†’ the same `MatchBonusCatalogSO` assigned to MatchManager._bonusCatalog.

3. No new SO assets needed â€” reuses the MatchBonusCatalogSO from T082.

**MatchEndBonus wiring (T082) â€” Editor-session steps:**
1. Create BonusCondition SO assets: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ BonusCondition.
   Suggested starter conditions:
   - "Perfect Shield": NoDamageTaken, Threshold=0, BonusAmount=100 (win without any damage taken)
   - "Speed Run": WonUnderDuration, Threshold=30, BonusAmount=75 (win in under 30 seconds)
   - "Destroyer": DamageDealtExceeds, Threshold=80, BonusAmount=50 (deal at least 80 damage)
   - "Efficiency Master": DamageEfficiency, Threshold=0.8, BonusAmount=60 (80%+ efficiency ratio)
2. Create MatchBonusCatalog SO: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ MatchBonusCatalog.
   Add the BonusCondition SOs to the _conditions list.
3. In the Arena scene, open MatchManager and assign the MatchBonusCatalog SO to `_bonusCatalog`.
   The bonus is evaluated in EndMatch() after per-match stats are known and before the wallet
   is credited, so currencyEarned in the MatchRecord reflects the bonus.
4. Optionally wire the PostMatchController to display bonus info (extend ShowResults() to
   iterate MatchBonusCatalogSO and show which conditions were met â€” UI-only edit, no physics).

**ArenaSelection wiring (T081) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ new, first priority
1. Create SO assets:
   - `ArenaPresetsConfig`: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Arena â–¶ ArenaPresetsConfig.
     Add one `ArenaPreset` entry per arena layout, each pointing to an `ArenaConfig` SO.
   - `SelectedArenaSO`: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Arena â–¶ SelectedArena.
     Create a `VoidGameEvent` SO for `_onArenaSelected` (optional, for reactive UI).
2. In the pre-match lobby scene, add `ArenaSelectionController` MB to any panel GameObject:
   - Assign `_presets` â†’ the ArenaPresetsConfig SO above.
   - Assign `_selectedArena` â†’ the SelectedArenaSO above.
   - Assign `_prevButton` / `_nextButton` â†’ cycle buttons (or wire onClick in Inspector).
   - Assign `_nameLabel` (optional Text) â€” shows the current arena's display name.
3. In the Arena scene, open `ArenaManager` and assign `_selectedArena` â†’ same SelectedArenaSO.
   - Leave `_arenaConfig` assigned as the fallback for play-testing without the lobby.
4. In the Arena scene, open `MatchManager` and assign `_selectedArena` â†’ same SelectedArenaSO.
   - `record.arenaIndex` will now be populated automatically from `ArenaConfig.ArenaIndex`.
   - Leave `ArenaConfig._arenaIndex` set per SO (e.g. 0 = Factory, 1 = Wasteland, 2 = Colosseum).

**CountdownManager wiring (T080) â€” Editor-session steps:** â†گ new, first priority
1. In the Arena scene, remove (or disable) the existing MatchStarter component.
2. Add `CountdownManager` to the same Arena-scene GameObject (e.g., GameManager).
3. Create an IntGameEvent SO: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Events â–¶ IntGameEvent.
   Name it "CountdownTickEvent". Assign to `CountdownManager._onCountdownTick`.
4. Create a VoidGameEvent SO: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Events â–¶ VoidGameEvent.
   Name it "CountdownCompleteEvent". Assign to `CountdownManager._onCountdownComplete`.
5. Assign the existing MatchStarted VoidGameEvent SO to `CountdownManager._matchStartedEvent`
   (same SO used by MatchManager, MatchFlowController, ArenaManager, PauseManager, CombatHUDController).
6. For the countdown UI panel, add `MatchCountdownController` to any persistent Canvas GameObject.
   - Assign `_onCountdownTick` â†’ CountdownTickEvent SO.
   - Assign `_onCountdownComplete` â†’ CountdownCompleteEvent SO.
   - Assign `_countdownPanel` â†’ the root GameObject of your countdown panel.
   - Assign `_countdownText` â†’ the UnityEngine.UI.Text component for the number/label.
   - Leave `_fightDisplaySeconds` at 1.0 s (or tune as desired).
7. Leave `CountdownManager._countdownFrom` = 3, `_tickInterval` = 1 s, `_initialDelay` = 0.1 s
   for a standard 3-second countdown.

**MatchRewardConfig wiring (T079) â€” Editor-session steps:**
1. Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ MatchRewardConfig.
   Set BaseWinReward (e.g. 200), ConsolationReward (e.g. 50), RoundDuration (e.g. 120 s).
2. In the Arena scene, open MatchManager and assign the asset to the new `_rewardConfig` field.
   The per-component _roundDuration / _winReward / _lossConsolationReward fields become inactive
   fallbacks; you may leave them at their current values for documentation purposes.
3. To A/B test different balance presets without scene changes, swap the _rewardConfig asset reference.

**Remaining work (Editor-session only â€” cannot be done by a remote agent):**

### Recommended first step: run SceneWiringValidator
Open the Arena scene â†’ Tools â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Scene Wiring Validator â†’ Scan Scene.
The tool will list every null SO reference across all BattleRobots components and let you click-to-select each one. Use the list below as your authoritative wiring guide.

### Running the test suite
Open the project in Unity â†’ Window â–¶ General â–¶ Test Runner â†’ EditMode tab â†’ Run All.
All 849 tests should pass without scene setup (they use `ScriptableObject.CreateInstance` and `Application.persistentDataPath`).

### Notification toast wiring (new â€” T072) â†گ first priority

1. Create SO assets:
   - `NotificationQueueSO`: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ NotificationQueueSO.
     One global instance.
   - Create a VoidGameEvent SO for `_onNotificationEnqueued` (or reuse an existing spare event).
   - Assign the VoidGameEvent to `NotificationQueueSO._onNotificationEnqueued`.

2. Assign the NotificationQueueSO to:
   - `AchievementManager._notificationQueue` â€” forwards achievement-unlock toasts.
   (Add additional producers as desired: MatchManager level-up bridge, etc.)

3. For the toast panel, add `NotificationController` MB to any persistent Canvas GO and wire:
   - `_queue`                    â†’ the NotificationQueueSO asset (required)
   - `_onNotificationEnqueued`   â†’ the same VoidGameEvent SO above (required)
   - `_notificationPanel`        â†’ the root GameObject of the toast panel (optional)
   - `_titleText`                â†’ the Text component for the notification headline (optional)
   - `_bodyText`                 â†’ the Text component for the notification body (optional)
   The panel auto-shows/hides via SetActive; `WaitForSecondsRealtime` keeps it visible
   even while the game is paused (Time.timeScale == 0).

### Career Stats wiring (new â€” T071) â†گ first priority

1. Create SO asset via Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ PlayerCareerStatsSO.
   One global instance.  Assign a VoidGameEvent SO to `_onStatsUpdated` if you want any
   UI panel to react in real time (e.g. a profile screen that refreshes after each match).

2. Assign the PlayerCareerStatsSO to:
   - `GameBootstrapper._careerStats`  â€” rehydrates from disk on startup.
   - `MatchManager._careerStats`      â€” accumulates damage/currency/playtime each EndMatch.

3. For the career stats panel, add `CareerStatsController` MB to any Canvas GameObject and wire:
   - `_careerStats`           â†’ the PlayerCareerStatsSO asset (required)
   - `_onStatsUpdated`        â†’ the VoidGameEvent SO from PlayerCareerStatsSO._onStatsUpdated
   Optional win-rate / streak / level sources:
   - `_playerAchievements`    â†’ PlayerAchievementsSO asset (enables _matchesPlayedText, _winsText, _winRateText)
   - `_winStreak`             â†’ WinStreakSO asset (enables _bestStreakText)
   - `_playerProgression`     â†’ PlayerProgressionSO asset (enables _levelText)
   Optional Text label refs (each silently skipped if null):
   - `_matchesPlayedText`, `_winsText`, `_winRateText`
   - `_damageDealtText`, `_damageTakenText`, `_currencyEarnedText`, `_playtimeText`
   - `_bestStreakText`, `_levelText`

4. SaveData backwards-compatibility: the four new fields
   (`careerDamageDealt`, `careerDamageTaken`, `careerCurrencyEarned`, `careerPlaytimeSeconds`)
   default to 0, so existing save files load cleanly with zero career totals.

### Achievement System wiring (new â€” T069) â†گ first priority

1. Create SO assets:
   - `AchievementCatalogSO`: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ AchievementCatalogSO
   - `PlayerAchievementsSO`: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ PlayerAchievementsSO
   - One or more `AchievementDefinitionSO` assets per achievement you want in the game.
     Example: id="first_win", trigger=MatchWon, targetCount=1, rewardCredits=100.

3. Add an `AchievementManager` MB to any persistent GameObject (e.g. the same root as GameBootstrapper).
   Wire the mandatory fields:
   - `_catalog`            â†’ AchievementCatalogSO asset
   - `_playerAchievements` â†’ PlayerAchievementsSO asset
   Wire optional trigger sources (skip any trigger type you don't use):
   - `_winStreak`           â†’ WinStreakSO asset
   - `_playerProgression`   â†’ PlayerProgressionSO asset
   - `_playerPartUpgrades`  â†’ PlayerPartUpgrades asset
   - `_matchResult`         â†’ MatchResultSO asset (blackboard â€” same one MatchManager writes)
   Wire event channels:
   - `_onMatchEnded`        â†’ MatchEnded VoidGameEvent SO
   - `_onLevelUp`           â†’ LevelUp VoidGameEvent SO (from PlayerProgressionSO)
   - `_onUpgradesChanged`   â†’ UpgradesChanged VoidGameEvent SO (from PlayerPartUpgrades)
   - `_onStreakChanged`      â†’ StreakChanged VoidGameEvent SO (from WinStreakSO)
   Optionally wire `_playerWallet` to grant credits on unlock.

4. Assign the PlayerAchievementsSO to `GameBootstrapper._playerAchievements`.

5. (Optional) Subscribe a UI element to `PlayerAchievementsSO._onAchievementUnlocked`
   and read `LastUnlockedId` to display a toast notification.

   Wire required fields:

   - `_catalog`              â†’ AchievementCatalogSO asset
   - `_playerAchievements`   â†’ PlayerAchievementsSO asset
   Wire optional progress sources:
   - `_winStreak`            â†’ WinStreakSO asset  (required for WinStreak progress display)
   - `_playerProgression`    â†’ PlayerProgressionSO asset  (required for ReachLevel progress display)
   - `_playerPartUpgrades`   â†’ PlayerPartUpgrades asset  (required for PartUpgraded progress display)
   Wire event channel:

     (auto-refreshes panel on each new unlock)

### WinStreakSO wiring (new â€” T067) â†گ first priority

### PlayerProgressionSO wiring (new â€” T068) â†گ first priority
This adds XP-based player levelling visible on the Main Menu and post-match screen.

1. Create SO asset via Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ PlayerProgressionSO.
   Set `_maxLevel` (default 10). Assign a VoidGameEvent SO to `_onLevelUp` and an
   IntGameEvent SO to `_onXPGained` if you want HUD widgets to react.

2. Assign the PlayerProgressionSO to:
   - `GameBootstrapper._playerProgression`
   - `MatchManager._playerProgression`

3. MatchManager calls `XPRewardCalculator.CalculateMatchXP()` automatically at match end:
   - Win:  base 100 XP + 1 per 5 s of fight + 10 أ— min(streak, 5)
   - Loss: base 25 XP + same duration/streak bonuses
   XP and Level are persisted to `SaveData.playerTotalXP` / `SaveData.playerLevel`.

4. For the HUD level display, add `PlayerLevelController` MB to any Canvas GameObject and wire:
   - `_progression` â†’ same PlayerProgressionSO asset
   - `_onLevelUp`   â†’ the VoidGameEvent SO above
   - `_onXPGained`  â†’ the IntGameEvent SO above
   - `_levelLabel`  (optional Text) â€” shows "Level N" or "Level MAX"
   - `_xpLabel`     (optional Text) â€” shows "N / M XP" or "MAX" at max level
   - `_xpFillImage` (optional Image, type Filled) â€” fill amount drives XP bar [0, 1]
This deepens the economy loop with a consecutive-win bonus and displays it on the post-match screen.

1. Create SO asset via Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ WinStreakSO.
   One global instance â€” assign `_onStreakChanged` VoidGameEvent if you want any system to react.

2. Assign the WinStreakSO to:
   - `GameBootstrapper._winStreak`
   - `MatchManager._winStreak`
   - `PostMatchController._winStreak` (optional)

3. Optionally, add a `Text` UI element to the PostMatchController panel and assign it to
   `PostMatchController._streakText`. ShowResults() will display:
   - `"Win Streak: N!"` when the player is on an active streak (CurrentStreak > 0).
   - `"Best Streak: N"` when the current streak is 0 (shows their all-time high).

4. MatchManager will automatically apply the streak bonus to win rewards:
   `reward = baseWinReward أ— (1.0 + 0.1 أ— min(streak, 5))` â€” capped at +50 %.
   Loss consolation reward is never boosted.

### MatchStatisticsSO wiring (T066)
This adds accurate per-hit damage tracking to the post-match results screen.

1. Create SO asset via Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ MatchStatisticsSO.
   One global instance â€” no fields to set in Inspector.

2. In the Arena scene, add two `DamageGameEventListener` components (on any persistent GO):
   - **Listener A** (player attacks):
     - `Event` â†’ the DamageGameEvent SO that the **enemy's** `DamageReceiver` listens to
       (i.e. the channel your `RobotAIController.FireAttack()` raises).
     - `Response (UnityEvent<DamageInfo>)` â†’ `MatchStatisticsSO.RecordDamageDealt(DamageInfo)`.
   - **Listener B** (enemy attacks):
     - `Event` â†’ the DamageGameEvent SO that the **player's** `DamageReceiver` listens to.
     - `Response (UnityEvent<DamageInfo>)` â†’ `MatchStatisticsSO.RecordDamageTaken(DamageInfo)`.

3. Assign the MatchStatisticsSO to `MatchManager._matchStatistics`.
   EndMatch() will now use `TotalDamageDealt/TotalDamageTaken` instead of the
   health-difference approximation.

4. Optionally, in the Arena Canvas, add `Text` fields to the PostMatchController panel and
   assign them to `PostMatchController._damageDoneText` and `_damageTakenText`.
   ShowResults() will format them as "Damage Dealt: N" / "Damage Taken: N".

### PartUpgradeSystem wiring (new â€” T057) â†گ next priority
This adds per-part upgrade tiers to the economy loop. Create the following SO assets and wire one upgrade panel per part row in the LoadoutBuilder or Shop scenes.

1. Create SO assets via Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy:
   - `PartUpgradeConfig` â€” one global instance.
     Set `_maxTier` (e.g. 3), `_tierCosts` length = maxTier (e.g. [100, 250, 500]),
     `_tierStatMultipliers` length = maxTier+1 (e.g. [1.0, 1.1, 1.25, 1.5]).
   - `PlayerPartUpgrades` â€” one global instance.
     Assign a `VoidGameEvent` SO to `_onUpgradesChanged` ("UpgradesChanged").
   - Assign `PlayerPartUpgrades` to `GameBootstrapper._playerPartUpgrades`.

2. In the shop or loadout scene, add `UpgradeManager` MB to any persistent GameObject and wire:
   - `_wallet` â†’ same PlayerWallet SO as ShopManager.
   - `_upgrades` â†’ the PlayerPartUpgrades SO above.
   - `_upgradeConfig` â†’ the PartUpgradeConfig SO above.
   - `_onUpgradeCompleted` â†’ a VoidGameEvent SO ("UpgradeCompleted").

3. For each upgradeable part row in the UI, add `UpgradeController` MB and wire:
   - `_upgradeManager` â†’ the UpgradeManager MB above.
   - `_upgradeConfig` â†’ same PartUpgradeConfig SO.
   - `_onUpgradesChanged` â†’ the UpgradesChanged VoidGameEvent SO.
   - `_tierLabel` (optional Text) â€” shows "âک…âک…âک†" style tier display or "MAX".
   - `_costLabel` (optional Text) â€” shows "Cost: 250" or "MAX".
   - `_upgradeButton` (optional Button) â€” calls UpgradePart on click; auto-wired in Awake.
   - Call `Setup(partDefinition)` from the parent row controller to bind the part.

4. Upgrade-aware stats preview in LoadoutBuilderController:
   - Add `_playerPartUpgrades` (PlayerPartUpgrades) and `_upgradeConfig` (PartUpgradeConfig)
     optional fields to `LoadoutBuilderController`.
   - Pass them to the 4-arg `RobotStatsAggregator.Compute()` overload in the stats-preview
     block inside `ConfirmLoadout()` (or wherever stats are displayed).
   - If null, the base 2-arg overload is used automatically (backwards-compatible).

5. SaveData backwards-compatibility: The two new fields (`upgradePartIds`, `upgradePartTierValues`)
   are initialised to empty lists, so existing save files load cleanly with zero upgrade data.

### DifficultySelection wiring (new â€” T056)
This adds a player-controlled difficulty picker to the pre-match flow.
1. Create SO assets via Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ AI:
   - `DifficultyPresetsConfig` â€” add one `DifficultyPreset` entry per difficulty level
     (e.g. "Easy" / "Normal" / "Hard"), each pointing to a `BotDifficultyConfig` SO.
   - `SelectedDifficulty` (SelectedDifficultySO) â€” one global instance shared across scenes.
2. On the pre-match lobby panel, add `DifficultySelectionController` MB and wire:
   - `_presets` â†’ the DifficultyPresetsConfig SO above.
   - `_selectedDifficulty` â†’ the SelectedDifficulty SO above.
   - `_prevButton` / `_nextButton` â†’ the cycle buttons.
   - `_nameLabel` (optional) â†’ a Text showing the current preset name.
3. On each enemy `RobotAIController` in the Arena scene, assign:
   - `_selectedDifficulty` â†’ the same SelectedDifficulty SO.
   When non-null and `Current != null`, this overrides the inspector `_difficultyConfig`
   field at Awake time â€” no per-robot Inspector changes needed for difficulty switching.
4. Optionally keep `RobotAIController._difficultyConfig` assigned as a fallback.
   If `_selectedDifficulty` is not wired (or `Current` is null), the inspector field is used.

### LoadoutBuilder wiring (new â€” T048) â†گ next priority after CombatStatsApplicator
This is the pre-match assembly screen. Create a new scene or panel in the Main Menu / pre-arena flow:
1. Create a "LoadoutSlot" prefab:
   - Attach `LoadoutSlotController` MB.
   - Assign optional UI refs: `_categoryLabel` (Text), `_partNameLabel` (Text),
     `_partDescLabel` (Text), `_thumbnailImage` (Image), `_prevButton` (Button), `_nextButton` (Button).
   - Wire `_prevButton.onClick â†’ LoadoutSlotController.PreviousPart` (or leave for Awake auto-wire).
   - Wire `_nextButton.onClick â†’ LoadoutSlotController.NextPart`.
2. On the loadout panel root, add `LoadoutBuilderController` MB and assign:
   - `_playerInventory` â†’ same PlayerInventory SO as GameBootstrapper.
   - `_playerLoadout` â†’ same PlayerLoadout SO as GameBootstrapper + MatchFlowController.
   - `_shopCatalog` â†’ same ShopCatalog SO as ShopManager.
   - `_robotDefinition` â†’ the player robot's RobotDefinition SO.
   - `_onInventoryChanged` â†’ same VoidGameEvent SO as PlayerInventory._onInventoryChanged.
   - `_slotRowPrefab` â†’ the LoadoutSlot prefab from step 1.
   - `_slotContainer` â†’ a ScrollRect Content Transform (VerticalLayoutGroup recommended).
   - `_confirmButton` â†’ a "Confirm Build" Button (or wire onClick â†’ ConfirmLoadout() in Inspector).
   - Optionally: `_healthText`, `_speedText`, `_damageText`, `_armorText` for live stats preview.
3. `ConfirmLoadout()` writes to `PlayerLoadout` **and** persists to disk automatically.
   Call it when the player presses "Enter Arena" or "Confirm Build".

### MatchFlowController loadout bridge wiring (new â€” T047)
In the Arena scene, open MatchFlowController and set the three optional loadout fields:
- `_playerLoadout` â†’ same PlayerLoadout SO used by LoadoutBuilderController.
- `_shopCatalog` â†’ same ShopCatalog SO.
- `_playerAssembler` â†’ the RobotAssembler on the **player** robot root.
  (The player assembler may also appear in `_assemblers` â€” that is fine, the override check
   routes it through `AssembleFromCatalog` instead of `Assemble`.)
When all three are assigned, the player robot rebuilds its equipped parts from the saved
loadout on every `MatchStarted` event. Enemy assemblers always use `Assemble()`.

### CombatStatsApplicator wiring (new â€” T045) â†گ highest priority
Add `CombatStatsApplicator` MB to each robot root GameObject in the Arena scene.
Wire the following fields:
- `_matchStartedEvent` â†’ same MatchStarted VoidGameEvent SO as MatchManager uses.
- `_robotDefinition` â†’ the chassis RobotDefinition SO for this robot.
- `_assembler` â†’ the RobotAssembler on the same GameObject.
- `_health` â†’ the robot's HealthSO asset (must be unique per robot).
- `_locomotion` (optional) â†’ the RobotLocomotionController on the same root.
- `_aiController` (optional, enemy robots only) â†’ the RobotAIController.
- `_damageReceiver` (optional) â†’ the DamageReceiver on the same root.

**Execution order:** `CombatStatsApplicator` has `DefaultExecutionOrder(10)`.
`MatchFlowController` (order 0) calls `Assemble()` first via its MatchStarted callback,
so `GetEquippedParts()` returns the live part list when `ApplyStats()` fires.

**PartDefinition Inspector:** Open each PartDefinition SO and set the "Combat Stats" fields
(`healthBonus`, `speedMultiplier`, `damageMultiplier`, `armorRating`) per part.

### PlayerLoadout wiring (new â€” T044)
- Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ PlayerLoadout (one global instance).
- Create a VoidGameEvent SO ("LoadoutChanged") and assign to `PlayerLoadout._onLoadoutChanged`.
- Assign the same PlayerLoadout SO to `GameBootstrapper._playerLoadout`.
- Call `PlayerLoadout.SetLoadout(assembler.GetEquippedPartIds())` after the player confirms their build in the pre-match assembly UI to persist the loadout for the next session.
- On match start, pass `PlayerLoadout.EquippedPartIds` to `RobotAssembler.Assemble()` to restore the saved build automatically.

### GameSettings wiring (new â€” T042)
- Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ GameSettings (one global instance).
- Create a VoidGameEvent SO ("SettingsChanged") and assign to `GameSettingsSO._onSettingsChanged`.
- Assign the **same** GameSettingsSO asset to:
  - `GameBootstrapper._gameSettings`
  - `AudioManager._settings`
  - `SettingsController._settings` (on any settings panel GO)
- On each settings panel, add `SettingsController` MB and assign the three optional Sliders
  (min 0, max 1). Settings persist automatically when the panel is hidden.
- `AudioManager` will scale all SFX volume by `EffectiveSfxVolume` (master أ— sfx) automatically.

### SceneRegistry wiring (new â€” T034)
- Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Core â–¶ SceneRegistry (one global instance).
- Set `_mainMenuSceneName`, `_arenaSceneName`, `_shopSceneName` to match exact Build Settings scene names.
- Assign the **same** SceneRegistry SO to:
  - `MainMenuController._sceneRegistry`
  - `PostMatchController._sceneRegistry`
  - `PauseMenuController._sceneRegistry`
- If left null, each controller falls back to hard-coded defaults ("MainMenu", "Arena", "Shop") â€” safe for initial testing.

### StarterInventoryConfig wiring (new â€” T030)
- Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ StarterInventoryConfig.
- Populate `_starterPartIds` with the IDs of parts new players should receive (must match PartDefinition.PartId exactly).
- Assign the SO to `GameBootstrapper._starterConfig`.
- On first launch (empty inventory), the bootstrapper unlocks and persists all starters automatically.
- Leave `_starterConfig` null to skip starter distribution (backwards-compatible).

### ShopCatalogView wiring (new â€” T029)
- Create a shop-row prefab with `ShopItemController` MB attached. Assign UI refs in the prefab Inspector:
  `_nameLabel` (Text), `_costLabel` (Text), `_descriptionLabel` (Text, optional),
  `_thumbnail` (Image, optional), `_buyButton` (Button), `_ownedBadge` (GameObject, optional).
- Wire `_buyButton.onClick â†’ ShopItemController.OnBuyClicked` in the prefab Inspector.
- On the shop panel GameObject, add `ShopCatalogView` MB and assign:
  - `_shopManager` â†’ the ShopManager in the scene
  - `_itemPrefab` â†’ the shop-row prefab above
  - `_itemContainer` â†’ the ScrollRect Content Transform (VerticalLayoutGroup recommended)
  - `_onInventoryChanged` â†’ same VoidGameEvent SO as PlayerInventory._onInventoryChanged
  - `_onBalanceChanged` â†’ same IntGameEvent SO as PlayerWallet._onBalanceChanged
- ShopCatalogView will instantiate one row per PartDefinition in the ShopCatalog and keep all rows in sync automatically.

### PlayerInventory wiring (new â€” T028)
- Create SO asset: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ Economy â–¶ PlayerInventory (one global instance).
- Assign the **same** SO asset to `GameBootstrapper._playerInventory` AND `ShopManager._inventory`.
- Create a VoidGameEvent SO ("InventoryChanged") and assign to `PlayerInventory._onInventoryChanged`.
- Wire the same "InventoryChanged" SO to `ShopCatalogView._onInventoryChanged`.

### BotDifficultyConfig wiring (optional)
- Create SO assets: Assets â–¶ Create â–¶ BattleRobots â–¶ AI â–¶ BotDifficultyConfig (Easy / Normal / Hard presets).
- Assign the desired SO to `RobotAIController._difficultyConfig` on enemy robots in the Arena scene.
- Leave null to use per-component inspector values directly (backwards-compatible).
- Suggested Easy preset: detectionRange 8, attackRange 2, attackDamage 5, cooldown 2.0, speed 0.7.
- Suggested Hard preset: detectionRange 22, attackRange 4, attackDamage 18, cooldown 0.5, speed 1.5.

### Arena Scene wiring
- **MatchStarter** *(new â€” add to GameManager GO)*: assign `_matchStartedEvent` (MatchStarted VoidGameEvent SO). Set `_startDelay = 0.1` to let AB settle.
- ArenaManager: assign ArenaConfig SO; populate _robotRoots list
- MatchManager: assign _playerHealth / _enemyHealth HealthSOs, _playerWallet SO, _onMatchEnded VoidGameEvent, _onTimerUpdated FloatGameEvent, _onWinJingle / _onLossJingle AudioEvent SOs, **_matchResult MatchResultSO**, **_playerAssembler RobotAssembler**
- MatchFlowController: assign _matchStartedEvent, _matchEndedEvent SO channels; _playerRobotRoot; _cameraRig; populate _assemblers, _aiControllers, _locomotionControllers
- RobotAssembler (on each robot root): assign _robotDefinition, configure _slotMounts (slotId â†” child Transform), assign _equippedParts
- RobotLocomotionController (player robot): _isPlayerControlled = true
- RobotAIController (enemy robots): assign _locomotion, _damageEvent, tune _detectionRange / _attackRange
- CameraRig + CameraShake (Main Camera): assign _target (player robot root); wire _shakeEvents to player HealthSO._onDeath and enemy HealthSO._onDeath
- **PauseManager**: assign _onMatchStarted, _onMatchEnded, _onPaused, _onResumed VoidGameEvent SOs
- **PauseMenuController**: assign _pausePanel, _pauseManager, _onPaused, _onResumed; wire Resume + QuitToMenu buttons
- **CombatHUDController**: assign _hudRoot, _timerText, _playerHealthSlider, _enemyHealthSlider, _playerHealth SO, _enemyHealth SO; wire _onMatchStarted, _onMatchEnded, _onTimerUpdated FloatGameEvent, _onPlayerHealthChanged / _onEnemyHealthChanged (HealthSO._onHealthChanged FloatGameEvent SOs)
- **PostMatchController**: assign _matchResult MatchResultSO, _resultPanel, text fields; assign _onMatchEnded; wire PlayAgain + MainMenu buttons; set _arenaSceneName / _mainMenuSceneName

### ShopUI Scene wiring
- ShopManager â†گ ShopCatalog SO + PlayerWallet SO; buy buttons onClick â†’ ShopManager.BuyPart(partDef)
- IntGameEventListener â†’ wallet Text display

### MatchHistoryController wiring (new â€” T040)
- Create a "HistoryRow" prefab. Attach `MatchHistoryRowController` MB.
  In the prefab Inspector assign optional Text refs:
  `_outcomeText` ("WIN"/"LOSS"), `_durationText` (MM:SS), `_rewardText` (+200),
  `_dateText` (e.g. "Apr 10, 2026").
- On the panel that should show match history (Main Menu or Post-Match screen):
  - Add `MatchHistoryController` MB.
  - Assign `_rowPrefab` â†’ the HistoryRow prefab above.
  - Assign `_listContainer` â†’ a ScrollRect Content Transform (VerticalLayoutGroup recommended).
  - Set `_maxDisplayCount` (default 10).
  - Optionally assign `_onMatchEnded` â†’ same VoidGameEvent SO as MatchManager._onMatchEnded
    so the list auto-refreshes after each match without a scene reload.
- `PopulateHistory()` is also safe to call from a Button.onClick event.

### VFX wiring
- Create spark and explosion ParticleSystem prefabs
- ImpactVFXHandler._damageEvent â†’ DamageGameEvent SO; assign spark ParticlePool
- DestructionVFXHandler._deathEvent â†’ per-robot HealthSO._onDeath VoidGameEvent; assign explosion ParticlePool
- AudioManager: assign and wire AudioEvent SOs to AudioManager pool

**Architecture notes for next agent / Editor operator:**
- `MatchStarter` is the ONLY component that raises MatchStarted. Place it in the Arena scene on a persistent GO; set `_startDelay = 0.1` (gives ArticulationBody one fixed-update to settle before locomotion begins).
- `MatchManager._matchResult` must be assigned the same **MatchResultSO** asset that `PostMatchController._matchResult` references â€” they share the same blackboard.
- `MatchManager._playerAssembler` is the `RobotAssembler` on the player robot root. Enemy assemblers do not need to be wired here.
- `CombatHUDController._onPlayerHealthChanged` = `PlayerHealthSO._onHealthChanged` FloatGameEvent asset. Same pattern for enemy.
- `CombatHUDController._onTimerUpdated` = same asset as `MatchManager._onTimerUpdated`.
- `PauseManager` must appear in the scene to handle `Time.timeScale`. Wire its output channels to `PauseMenuController`.
- `CameraShake` must sit on the **same GameObject** as `CameraRig` (or a parent); `DefaultExecutionOrder(100)` ensures it runs after CameraRig's LateUpdate.
- `MatchFlowController` subscribes to SO channels via `RegisterCallback` (not VoidGameEventListener component); no additional listener components needed.
- All SO channels (MatchStarted, MatchEnded) must be the **same asset references** across MatchStarter, MatchManager, ArenaManager, MatchFlowController, PauseManager, CombatHUDController, and PostMatchController.
